I examine them and found in one 18 ounces weighing, and in the other 6 ounces., and the work of the incision is that you examine if the patient's humors are moist, and the color of the arterial root is pale and moist and of subtle origin; if you touch with a large spatula, and let the fire cautery be present.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	Because when cutting, there often come great streams of blood, and if you do not stop them, then hasten to cauterize; and if you see the patient is frightened and afraid of the incision with iron, take a well-made thread, and tie off the arterial root as we have said, and let it be for two days; and then restrain, and do not cease from constricting the thread until it touches the root, and thus relieves the pain; and if the roots are large, fear not to copiously cauterize around the belly, but you can well cauterize most of it, then cauterize so it does not return; then cure the wound, and beware that you do not cauterize the thread which is of false color and poor sense and little regard.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an encrusted abscess, and I will come to the treatment of encrusted abscess later on.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the swelling is full
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the abscess comes from cautery of a wound or a crack in the skin, and it is on the belly and in some of the buttons, as if it had in other routes, either from blood that flows from veins or arteries according to what is before, or from windiness; and if it is by the route of the skin and by the issue of the abscess, if the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the body, and it is a light thing without pain, and opens into diverse issues.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is by the exit of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when one presses with their fingers if it swells up, and then returns, and perhaps by chance it is severe, and greatly increases at the entrance of the bath and through strong labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light thing, and opens well when you press on it with your hand, it does not constrain at all; and if it is due to blood, it opens by these signs the large and hard abscesses, and is fixed according to a quantity; and if it is due to windiness, it is soft to the touch, and the works are that you examine if the appearance is due to the blood of the artery, or of the vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	It must be that you leave the treatment.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I have told you in this chapter on abscesses, for the artery and for the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is for the intestine or the bouillon, then it must be that you order the patient to hold his arm straight and extended, and mark a spot around the bouillon; then order him to put his hand between yours, and go around the place where you have marked the entire spatium; then bind it with a strong thread or a cord of strong silk firmly, and make sure the ligament is sound; then uncover half of the abscess extended over the ligament, and insert your finger, and feel the intestine; if you find it taken by the ligament, then release it, and put the intestine back in its proper place; and if you find the bouillon, take it to the groin, and cut away the excess flesh; and if the artery or vein is opposed, then go gently around, then return to your work and take two needles, and insert two strong threads, and insert the two needles into what you have made in a cross so that you make them pierce; then pull out the abscess in four places on the needles, and if you see it, remove the needles, and let the place heal as much as possible, and cut off the dead flesh by itself; or take care of it when it is subtle and putrid, then cure what must be cured, and drain the abscess as we have said; and extract the blood or moisture that you find, then cure the place of what must be cured, and sew up the place.
dou chancre	swollen tumor
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division the similarities of tumors, and how one should operate with medicines, and how one should eschew the cure with iron; and we say that the tumor grows in the marrow, and great caution is necessary in its cure, and the ancients say that when a tumor is in the body or where it can be rooted like a tumor which is in the veins, and in the arteries, and in similar places, and it should be totally removed when it is in its beginning; and when it is large and old, one should not approach it, for I do not know how to heal any of them; nor did anyone ever heal before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the operations, when it is in the body or where it can be removed, as we have said, is that you purge the patient of black bile; then make them healthier if they show manifest repletion, then perform the operation on the affected limb to do the surgery; then cut out the tumors and all parts, and remove all the bone without leaving anything behind; and let the blood flow freely, and hold the limb well in your hand or with something, and see that the blood does not flow contrary to the incision of the artery or vein, if you cauterize so that the wound is staunched; then cure another cure until they are healthy.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have said in the division the similarities of hydropsy, and in what manner the assembly of water is made, and the signs of each similarity, and the cure that is made by medicines, and that which is cured by iron: it is clarified solely; and one should not touch with iron in these two similarities: it is to know, tympanites and yposarche, for it is a mortal thing; therefore when you medicate this similarity of hydropsy called "clarified" by medicines, and the cure does not profit, if you see the patient is weak, or if they have another illness besides hydropsy, as in tumors and solutions of the belly and similar things; if one should not touch with iron, for there is doubt; and if you see the patient has strong virtue, and they have no other illness except hydropsy solely, and it is not too young nor too old, then one should operate: lift the patient straight up in your hands, and the ministers press the belly at the lowest part of the pis, then take the spinal spatula according to this form.
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let there be two incisions.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	At a point, and in no way should it be so internal that it cannot reach the intestine when thrust in, and it should not be blocked; then see if the dropsy is turned towards the intestines: if it is necessary to make an incision below the navel on the right side of the third rib; and if it is due to liver disease, let the incision be on the left side of the third rib; and if it is for the spleen, let it be on the right, and it is not necessary that the patient should gaze at the incision lest the superfluous liquids run to the weak spot; then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and the belly, and lift your hand to the entire space between the skin and the fascia as in scraping the quantity of a fingernail or an inch or so; then pierce the fascia until the space reaches the empty space, and it is the flow of water, then draw it back, and you throw away this instrument which is of this form.
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it is similar to a subtle silver tube, and it is of lead or tin alloy, and has small holes on the underside; and where one side costs three holes; and two on another side, and one on another; and the head is shaped like a pen, and this is the form of the incision that writers shape their pens with.
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	at the top is the almond-shaped (instrument), so that when the instruments come to the water, they immediately settle on the instrument; empty it now, removing half or a third part, because if you remove more than is necessary at that time, perhaps the patient will die from the resolution of their spirit's arm, or they will become numb, or approach death; but empty according to the quantity of its virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue of the malady signify, and its pulses; then pull out the instrument and hold the water, and it is held now by the cord that stops up the hole that is on the syringe, as I have spoken, that you pierce in this manner; then reintroduce the instrument the next day, if you see the patient suffering thus, and pull from the water a small quantity; do this every day, and guard against fooling around until it no longer remains but a little water.

And if you doubt about the patient, and you leave much of water, if the treatment of the grave or tomb is hot, and by much sweating or bath and in the sun, and you touch on drinking; and the treatment with drying medicines as long as it is healthy, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of water, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stopping of the rod
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	No time is born a child who does not have holes in the penis, or the hole is small, or it is not in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If you want to pierce them so that they do not have to perceive everything in the very subtle spatium, according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Then put or make holes I close subtly with a plank, and tie it thus for three or four days, and when he wants to urinate, if the closure is opened, and urinate, and then replace it; and by chance it does not close, because the urine that comes forth does not allow it to close.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	The place where the perforation is small, if it is medicated with a thick cloth of wool, as we have said, so it will enlarge.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have a perforation in their body are stricken, for none are born with a perforation at the head of the rod, because they cannot urinate before they lift their rod high; and they cannot be helped because the matter cannot reach to the marrow, and it is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of the work is that the patients sit bent over their back, with their head against the rod and their arm as long as a pen, so that the hole is in the middle, as it needs; and beware of the flow of blood that comes many times, and if it happens, then staunch the bleeding, and cure the wound until it is healthy.
des pustules de la verge	blisters of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times cysts come on the penis, and it is an appearance of ugly lichen; and there are malignant and non-malignant ones; if it is necessary that you take them with a very subtle onion, and scrape and clean all, then put on soft cotton in Egyptian ointment; then the treatment of ointment Diafinicon until it be healthy.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the ulcer is malignant, of foul color and putrid, then you must apply fire cautery to it.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have coupled it, and the ulcer is on the rod, and has a part inside the skin and a part outside, then you must remove the ulcer that is inside first; and when it is sewn, you must cure the outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you treat together, if it is not assured the head of the rod that it is not perceived, and comes blackness and corruption in its rod and in the conjunction; if it is necessary to expel all that is black and corrupted, then place it on the plaster made of honey and flour which is made from the scorched peel of grenade pomegranates and of veal, then treat with other treatments until it is healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if a flow of blood comes, then apply the lunar cautery in this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cauteries thus aid in two dispositions together: it is to know, at the flow of blood, and at the corruption; and if the head of the rod is corrupted and withdrawn, then it is necessary that you apply or conduct a vein of lead, and pierce the patient through; and when the skin is burned at the head of the rod which has happened to those who have not been circumcised, either by wound or by abscess, then it is necessary that you scrape with an instrument curved thus, so that the veins are disentangled, and the head of the rod is freed from all parts; and if this is a difficult thing to devise, then it is necessary that you scrape with a spatula around the head of the rod and of the skin; then you separate gently between two, and place a subtle drapery of linen in cold water, so that it does not burn again.
de la circoncision	of the circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not one of the less severe wounds; however when we perform this work of our will, and properly with children, it is necessary that we do the best work, and the lightest for salvation.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not circumcise their children, for they did not use it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	Because I wanted the largest part of the masters and surgeons who performed circumcisions around there, and with forces, and all in a new manner; if it happened that the courses because there are two tiles, and by chance if one covers on top and stays below.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or the recovery is covered, and the pain is double, and in the mending which is two fingers from the point of the limb; and in the mending of the ankle by chance the iron escapes, and corrupts the work, and many times it happens that they have no need of mending and I wanted.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	From the mending which is done with forces all the way to the thread of wire I have found the goodness of the experiment, because the forces cut just as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez. Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The shape of the forces at the cleansing is this: the two heads should be turned and should be cutting, and the heads should be as large as the equally-sized hands.

And if they trespass for three days, and that which is beneath the rod is inflamed, let it be until the apostemes of the wound are appeased, and lightly scrape off; if you touch it as you can move, and guard against the part of the rod, this will not harm.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Heal then the wound of sudden powder, that we have said or treated with powders, and if you touch with a gentle hand beyond measure, and it goes to the surface, it will not harm; heal then, as we have said, until it is healthy.
dou retenement de l’urine	due to retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief. des maladies de la vessie	of the diseases of the vein
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When blood or pus comes into the vein, where putrefaction is assembled, and you have seen to distill sharp points and medicines, if you make all the instrument called "clepsydra", and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	Here is the translation:

de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already said in the division the methods of stone, and the extraction along with medicines; and I said the difference between the stone in the kidney as it rains, and all the signs, and in which stone one must operate by cutting; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell you openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is in the bladder often affects children, and it's a sign that the water jumps from the bladder with similar subtlety; and it openly hurts, and grievously afflicts the penis, and many times then becomes inflamed; and most of these jumps are fundamentals; and it's easy to heal children until they are 12 years old, and it's very difficult in old age, and it's as if midway, for those who are between youth and old age; and it's easier to cure those who have large stones than those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, it is necessary first to clean the patient with a clyster, in order to expel all the bad humors that are in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it often hinders one from questioning the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet and make them bend over and move to the Dorsal region, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and it often falls down from the high part; then have them sit between your hands, prepared, and their hands are below their thighs, so that the bladder is entirely declined downwards; then question and touch inside; if you feel the stone in the space, hurry now to cut into the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not fall to the toucher from everything, if you moisten your right index finger with oil from your left hand, if the patient is weak, or your left hand, if the patient is young and accomplished; and put it in its foundation, and question the stone, and when you feel it at your finger, if you press it to the neck of the bladder; then press on your finger, and put it in the place where you see to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And instruct the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and instruct him to extend his right hand above the loins, and with his left hand remove the skin that is beneath the loins in the area where the waist is made; then he inserts the spatula, which is the form.
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And make an incision between the area that is between the hip and the fundament, not in the middle but on the side of the left thigh; and let it be straight on the stone, and both should be equally or fundamentally, and let the cutting be so large by default, and within it is narrow, according to the quantity of the stone, not too big; perhaps the pressure if both are in fundament, that it feels less labor; and know that there is a part of the stone where it has angles, and margins: if it is difficult to remove; and if it is a part that is underneath, similar to a pebble, and rounded, whose removal is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	If it has angles and margins, make the cutting larger; and if it does not come out, then you must extract from the tongs that are like a file at the head, to carefully extract the stone so it doesn't break; or you insert underneath an instrument subtle and curved at the head; and if you cannot engineer it thus, then enlarge the small hole, and if the blood does not flow, then extract with vitriol; and if there is more than one stone, then remove the largest first at the neck of the bladder, then cut above, then pull forcefully, and the small ones afterwards if there are many.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, it needs to be operated on, and to make a bigger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	Because these things happen to the patient: either he dies, or the urine comes out immediately because the wounds cannot close; but nevertheless make an effort to treat, or to remove the tendons, as much as you can treat them in pieces; and when you have accomplished your work, if you fill the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and hold it steady, and put on top a warm dressing in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold rose water, to calm the hot abscess; then resolve the patient's pain on his neck, and do not loosen the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you loosen it, rub very well the joint with oil and water, then apply the ointment of diyafinicon and ointment of basilicon, until it is healthy.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if hot abscesses come in the wound and corrode, and congealments of blood in the bladder, and thus retain the urine, which is known in such a way that without a sound with the urine: then put your finger in the wound, and extract that blood, for if it remains, it will corrode the bladder, and rot; then lift the wound with warm water and oil, and help in all ways that you know, as long as he may be healthy; and it is necessary that all the openings that you cure, that you bind the two thighs, and assemble the medicines on the place.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it is led by the rod, and fixed in, and the urine cannot flow out; if you cure this as I say thus, that you cut many times, it is excused from the cutting by this cure.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already proved it thus.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take a rod of iron in this form and it is fixed at three angles in the thigh.
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take the thread and wind it around the rod beneath the stone, so that it cannot come back into the bladder; then insert the instrument into the rod gently, until it reaches the stone; and turn the instrument with your hand in the stone little by little, until you can feel the stone from another part; if the urine comes soon, then press your hand on what remains of the stone which is within the rod.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is soon broken, and jumps out with the urine, and the patient is cured; and if you cannot do this because of some thing that defeats it, then thread beneath the stone and another above, then make the rod in the place of the stone between the two ligatures, then extract it forcibly, and untie the ligature, and cleanse the congealed blood which is in the wound; and cure until it is healthy.
de la piere des femmes	of the stones of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It is rare that a stone forms in women, and if it happens sometimes, the treatment is difficult, and is defended by three things: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman who knows well how to conceal herself as mirrors, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third way is that by chance one cannot find a woman well-versed in this art of hands; and the fourth way is that the skin of the woman is more prominent than the skin of the man, which allows for deeper cutting, and great fear there. And if you need to ascend to this, it is necessary that you take a wise woman knowing well, and touch the vein on, and if you do not find it, then ask I cast a subtle gaze; and present a wise old woman in the life of women, where a woman knows part of the art, and instructs her to do what you command regarding the inquiry into the skin; and look very well if the woman is virgin: then she needs to put her finger or foundation and seek the skin; and if she finds it, she constrains beneath her finger, and recommends that she puts her finger or with the patient, and presses her left hand on the bladder firmly.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	Here is the translation:
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	you examine the symptoms to know the issue.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the saneness (health) fails you, set on the vitriol ointment, and hold it for an hour until the saneness is restored; then return to your work, until the stone is broken, and use the instruments that I told you about in extracting the stone as men do to help you in your operation; and if the saneness fails you, and it's a blocked artery, set powder on the spot and use tourniquets and bandages, and don't start again, and leave the stone alone and don't disturb it anymore, lest by chance the patient dies; then cure the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is appeased, and the veins are purified, then return to your work, until the stone is loose.
de hernie carnouse	of a fleshy hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Fleshy hernia is nothing other than a gathering of moisture or white syrup, which is beneath the skin of the thighs, that contains the egg-white; and it is called "syphac", and sometimes is properly in the membrane of the egg-white, if one thinks it is another egg; and it is the skin of the thigh between the white syrup that we have said; and this has not happened little.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this limb is from weakness that comes to the joints, and it spreads that matter.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And often if there is percussion on the joints, and this moisture has many colors: either it's a declining color to yellowish, or without red, or black, or watery pale, and this happens more; and these are the signs of recognizing this assembly, for if it is white or yellow as we have said, it's a ripe abscess, I think it takes long as the figure of an egg, and doesn't open the joints, for it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if it has moisture in its own fabric, the abscesses are reconnected with part of the vein, and because of this people think that it's another vein; and if the moisture is between the skin of the joints and the white syrup, then he feels very well; therefore when you want to know the color of the moisture, you examine everything thoroughly, because its form is seen there beforehand.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what comes after the inner quarter, judge of what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we treat with iron, it is necessary that the patient be healthy according to his power and the fullness of his body; then he sits on his back, on something a little high, and much drapery is placed under him; then he sits on his left side, and instructs the minister to sit on his right, and stretches out the rod to one of the two hollow ribs of the joints; then take the spatula, and cut the skin of the joints all the way down to the white skin, making a straight incision in dividing the skin of the joints up to the white skin, and carefully stripping it away according to his power; then pierce the white skin plain with water at a large opening, and extract all the water, and then put on your onions, and let the skin heal above; and do not touch the joints, but only the skin; cut everything or in pieces very subtly, so that if you do not cut well, the water will return; and if the vein flows strongly into your work, then reset it in its place when you have completed the work of the skin; then assemble the two hollow ribs of the joints at one seam, then cure as for other wounds, until he is healthy.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the white spot corrupted by another disease, it is necessary that you lift the veins that are suspended, doubting the decormentation of blood; then cut the joint at all the suspension, and extract the white spot, and cure it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the wound is assembled in two parties together, know that these are two branches; if you join the other party as you did the first equalization, then suck out the blood, and put on the clean wound a layer of oil rose; and put beneath another layer of oil and wine, and put on the two bandages, and put above doubled drapery, and bind with all the ligature that is according to this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two bandages, and employ a layer of torn linen according to this resemblance and are assembled by stitching in the girdle of the arms, and one of the heads takes hold on the foundation just to the back, and another at the part of the handle; and another head on the two angles, and so is all assembled the restraint in the loop of the arm; and no medicine is this branch of cautery in the place of iron size, and it is that you take the subtle cautery tool, and join the skin of the bandages, and be careful as we have said, so that the white sap that contains the wound is discovered; if you take the cautery according to this form, and pierce that sap as on occasions, and scrape with this subtle cautery hot:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And examine the whole in every way that you can, as much as you stretch everything; and beware that the cautery does not touch the vein; and know that this work is more salvaging; and beware of the deterioration of blood, and worse than the operations of cutting; and if nothing makes you contrary, or abscess bursts or deteriorations of blood or another thing, so cure what makes you contrary, according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is fearful, and does not want to undergo this operation due to its horridness, then make a perforation, as I tell you, and it is that when you are well certain through the signs we have said that the aquose water is there, then seat the patient on a high chair; then pierce the abscess in the lower part of the whole spatula large, and put the perforation from the long cord of the body; and make the openings wide, so that all the water flows out; then put cotton on the wound, and bind it, and let it flow out all the remaining water, then cure until the wound is healthy; and if the white cloth does not allow the water to issue from the mouth of the wound, then you must insert a tube or instrument with which one draws out the water of the hydropics, in the shape that is described before; and enlarge the wound, and know that the water returns, and is assembled after six months or within a year, and when it is assembled as before, then the patient will pass their days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the groin
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Be aware that in the section of this arm there are many fearful dispositions, because it seems to me that some are worth leaving; and I will tell you about the work and the similar things of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say then that many abscesses come from corruption, and likewise from wounds; and it is in most cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	It is to know by the excess and bitterness of a sharp and acute [fever], which is spread through the veins, or from percussion; and it is the color of the abscess according to the color of the body; and there is no true pain, and it is a grievous abscess; and by chance some abscesses are greenish and livid, and of foul color, and sometimes they come from inflammation of an artery, or from swelling of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is from inflammation of an artery, it is known by the disposition of hot abscess, when you press it with your fingers; and it does not seem that you should touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	Here is the translation:
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the wound is suddenly swollen with these new flesh, then it is necessary to treat the wound, and the scalpel; and if it is attached to the syphac, or in that which is within the vessels, then it is necessary to deliver all that tension, and the scalpel rounds again.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the flesh is where the skin is behind, then it is necessary that you cut it all, and withdraw the vein, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the operations are completed, then apply the plaster of boiled linseed oil and wine, then heal with other treatments until it is healthy.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the groin
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	These are enclosed abscesses with an enclosure similar to a scorpion's sting, with the softening of the sides, and the patient suffers greatly when it bursts; and the treatment of this disease is very near just as frightening as this one before, and always we will describe the work of it, according to what the ancient ones did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	It is necessary to make the patient sit on the elevated seat, then apply the suspensor to the sides down to the two fingers, to all the vessels that are near the verge, and tighten the masters, and extend them firmly; then cut with a sharp spatula through the area where the vessels are uncovered, and then scrape away from each part, as we have said in the extraction of arteries that are in temples; then fix a double-threaded needle or where it has a double thread, and tie it to the first vein or where the vitellus has come, and re-tie it to the other head; then cut in a straight line according to the length of the body, and remove the corrupting humors; then treat the wound as the others, so that no vessel is injured, lest they worsen one of the sides; for by this means no harm comes, and if all vessels come together, it is necessary to treat the sides at all vessels; so that the eyes do not lose their nourishment through the incision of vessels, and dry up and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	of the treatment of this face
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	Here is the translation:
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac. de hernie carnouse	of a fleshy hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this case I never saw anyone who dared to make the treatment with iron.

And the old ones said that it is done like the ramice which is assembled on the face, in such a way that you bind the veins, after shaving lightly around the base; then cut into the middle, and treat the abscess with what opens, until the veins heal; and treat thus as we have said, until it is perfectly healthy.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Sometimes a rupture occurs in the groin, as we have said, and opens the veins; and does not descend into the intestines at all, and if it descends, it is little, and repairs itself every hour; and however if it lasts too long at this point, the wound or abscess grows, until the intestine descends; and this happens due to the extension of the syfac which is in the groin, as we have said, because it is stretched, then softened and enlarged the veins and opened; and the treatment is by cautery, as we have previously said; and sometimes it is treated with iron in this manner: and it is that the patient places himself on his back between your hands, then cuts the vein of the ruptured large intestine according to the quantity of three fingers; and then extracts the syfac which is under the skin that is swollen, then takes the remedy and puts it on the apparent vein of the syfac; and presses at the bottom of the belly, then cuts the two apparent veins of the syfac on the head of the remedy, and cuts one and the other; then extracts the head of the remedy, and does not cut any point of the syfac that does not stretch another thing, as I have made you know in the treatment of the ramice of the intestines; then treats by treating the wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the threads, if it is undamaged and cures the wound, so that it becomes healthy.

dou chastrement	two cauteries
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	I know that cauterization is commended in our law, and therefore it pleases me that I do not speak of it in this book; and it is not necessary to forbid it except by two means: one is that the masters respond when asked about the cure, and another, because we often have need of cauterization of certain beasts to help us, such as goat and sheep and cattle and other beasts.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say therefore that cauterization is performed according to two methods: either by attraction or by incision.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In that which we do by attraction, we make the beast sit in warm water, until the joint becomes softened and relaxed; then take them in your hand, until they are reset and you no longer feel them.

From the tailoring of stature: it is necessary that you hold the best, and press the skin of the thighs with your left hand, then suspend it, and cover each eye with a cop, when you have well examined them; and let no pouch of the subtle blood vessels and the subtle blood vessels that are under the veins; and this manner of tailoring is more suitable than that which is done by attraction, because at attraction something of the thighs may remain by chance, for which the best desires luxury; then heal the wound until it is healthy.
des hermofrodites	of hernias
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphroditism is according to two manners in men: one is that between the two thighs appears as if it were the figure of a woman's nature, where there are hairs, and sometimes it cuts off the urine.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other manner is in women, and has on the little finger as if a penis and two thighs.

And the treatment of the swelling and of the fame is that you cauterize all the affected places, and treat them as other wounds; in the second way, for men whose urine passes through the skin of their thighs, there is no cure.

A pustule is an affected place on the natural part, so much it is too ugly to behold; and some women have it as big as a hand, and that's the treatment.

de erratique	of scarifying
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Here is the translation:
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the symptoms are nearly apparent, then examine with your fingers or on the radius.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is a subtle swelling, and it is nearly at the liver, then hurry, and prepare thus: put your two index fingers together, and the woman should be on her back, spreading her legs; then bend the two fingers strongly, so that the subtle swelling is rounded, and covers the symptoms; then take a linen cloth, and moisten it in oil, and place it on the spot, and give the woman a hot bath each day, if she cannot sweat.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the swelling is hard and thick, then it is necessary that you apply cups to the spatium-like leaves of myrtle.

des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Embroilments are overgrowths of veins which lack normal accustomation, and when the embroilments are old they become hard; and we have already said in the division the similarities of these, and the signs, and I will tell you those that receive curation.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that embroilments and hardenings, when they are deeply rooted in the marrow, and they do not appear to sensation, if it is not a cure by iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those that are at the mouth of the marrow, which one can feel, are those that one can cure.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	It is necessary then that you put the woman in a cold house, then stretch out the tendons, and cover it with its roots, then sprinkle on medicines stopping blood flow, such as dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then bind her feet to the wall for an hour, then put her in cold water; and if the blood is removed, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate peel and gallic and similar things, and then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and vinegar, and make a plaster on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it sticks, that's good.

des apostemes de la marris	of the abscesses of the marrow
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many types of abscesses occur in the marrow, such as cancer and piercing abscesses and herpes and swellings and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscesses, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is necessary therefore that I describe in this treatise the hot abscess that occurs in the marrow, which is not among the abscesses that burst outward; and if you want to know the work of iron, look to see if the abscess is agitated at the beginning of its arrival, and full of bitterness and fever, and if it becomes red then you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Then do not hasten to pierce, but make the wound bigger so that the pain is alleviated; and then seat the patient on a stool, and have him lean against something or recline, and support himself on his back and bring his feet together as parts of a broken leg; and let his thighs be expanded, and put his arms under his knees, and bind them well with a linen bandage; then suck out the pus from the right side, and prepare the instrument by which one opens the mouth of the marrow, so that afterwards it takes shape; and you must see to arrange this instrument so that you make the first incision to know the depth of the marrow, lest what enters from the instrument does not go too far in and hurts the patient; and if the instruments are larger, then you must cover the depth of the marrow with drapery, so that the instrument does not grieve him; and you must put the horn of the instrument above, and hold the instrument.

And when the abscess opens, and one makes a fleshy wound on the hand, if it is necessary to cover the head with a spatula; and when the boil is emptied, if it is necessary to put ten moillies of oil rose or green oil in the wound, or to anoint the edge of the marrow and above the vein with a clean moillie; then one cures after two days of ointment, until it be sound; and often lift up the marrow and the wound by anointing with water and honey, and then with water or roots of lily and aristologe so be cured; then return to the ointment.

de l’enfantement	of the swelling

Here is the translation:

And if the two hands are too weak, it is necessary that you reset them lightly step by step; and if they cannot enter, place the woman on a chair, and lift her feet high up; then remove the chair from the ground, and hold the woman so she does not fall over; and if the hands cannot enter, and the infant dies, place the hands at the waist which is set before, and extract the infant, and reset equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	from the birth of the child on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes onto its feet, it is necessary to hold it high up; and then turn it little by little, until it is straightened; then take one of the feet and stretch it little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	When it falls just to the hips, instruct to take hold, and make it straighten with effort; if it falls weak, may God help.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not jump frequently as we have said, then it turns a little and a little, until it is according to the natural figure.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is lighter.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come forth as we have said, take a poultice of hot water, and oil of sesame, and melted gum, and crush everything in the mortar; and put it on the nature of the woman's womb inwardly and remove this ointment, then make her sit in warm water up to the ribs; and when she is softened underneath, make her wear a belt of myrrh, and put it underneath, and leave it for an hour; then make her sit on a chair, then make her lean back and hold her mouth and nose, and take her belly lightly, for the infant will now come forth.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	from the issue of the child on his knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the infant comes in this form, then put the basin under her hands little by little; then let it be seen on her neck, and let the feet hang down, and let it be laid out on the bed; and bend her hands little by little, and then take her hands on the belly, and remove the cushions from underneath, so that she is prepared below; and if the infant does not come forth, take its feet and move them gently, then move the belly upwards, then put your hands in; and bring the infant out little by little; and instruct the woman to push as much as the infant will come out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	from the delivery of the child who is coming out with one hand while
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.
