And if you cannot dislodge them within an hour, then put on the wound a poultice that induces suppuration, and let it be until the pus is formed among the bones, and then they will have less difficulty with the bones; and if it's a large bone, such as the leg or thigh, then remove as much of the corruption as possible until the blackness is entirely gone, then restore the wound; and if there is great part of the corrupted area, and it reaches almost to the marrow of the bone; then you must thoroughly clean and cover up to the corruption, and then cure until it is solidified; and I will tell you about a fistula that happened in my home on his leg, so that you take an example and aid in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	It was a young man around 30 years old, who had pain in his leg due to a cause that came from within the body, so much that the matter came to the leg, and it was inflamed with a large abscess, and there was no way to open it; but the foolish doctor operated so much on it that the abscess opened, and corroded a lot of matter, and became a fistula, and many doctors treated him for two years, and there was no skill in the art of hands, until I was called, and I saw his leg and the medicines with which he was being cured, and what corroded through the pores of the large body; and the body of the young man became red, and had a citrine color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I thrust a probe into one of these holes, and then explored all the holes, and found that one vein came against another from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I hurried then, and probed into one of the holes as far as I discovered a part of the bone, and found it corrupted and pierced, and the corruption went as far as the bone within; I saw what appeared to me of the corrupted bone, and thought that there was no other corruption except for the one I had seen; and I began to restore the wound with medicines through lengthy treatment, but could not succeed; and then I recommenced, and discovered the bone as before, and found the continued corruption in the bone, and saw it, and then removed it, and thought of suturing the limb; but I was unable to do so much that I probed into a palm of the bone, and treated it thoroughly throughout its entire mass, then restored it with medicines; and it was healed suddenly, and no longer needed to recommence the work except for the faintness of the patient, who could not suffer, and for the fear of death that I had of him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	Because the bloody evacuations often occur, but it was entirely healthy, and a hard crust formed on the bone, and was of good disposition and had no harm or contradiction in everything, neither to alleviate nor to come.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, you must treat it in this way: take a bandage, and bind it to the top of the bone that is open, and instruct him to stretch it upwards; and put another bandage, thicker than the first one, on the crust that is above the bone, and hold the top steady, so that you draw out the rotten flesh from below, and uncover the flesh on the bone where you see need to treat, so that the treatment does not spoil the flesh; and put a hot iron or a cup under the bone to clean out the rotten flesh; and continue treating until you can see and feel the corruption, and treat again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part, so uncover the entire flesh; then put fire underneath, and then move one part to the other to corrupt it, and be the surgeon of the length of the corruption I told you about; and if the corruption is in a joint, then cut into the corrupted joint, and move the bone or where it contains the other part; and if the corruption is in the continuation of two joints, then there is no other angle than to cut through; and if the corruption is on the hand or foot, it is very difficult, but you must inquire about that corrosion, how it appears to you; and consider it in all ways that you can, but do not let the vein or nerve contradict you; and know that the incision and the movements to cut into these bones are many, according to the arrangement of the bones and their appearance, and their thickness and subtlety, and their greatness and smallness, and their hardness; and for this reason it is necessary to adapt each instrument to its operation; and know that experience will show you the instrument you will need, according to your knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the methods of illnesses; if you prepare the instrument you will need according to what you have learned.
dou feu	with fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The heads perish either by internal cause or by external blow; and when you have medicated that corrosion through the treatment of medicines, and it does not benefit, then it is necessary to amputate that member up to where the corrosion comes from, so that the patient escapes death, or malice, which is greater, due to the defect of that member; and the signs are that the members turn black, as if they were burned by fire, and afterwards turn dark, since the corrosions of member into member spread throughout the body; if you hasten to amputate, and it is through the percussion of certain venomous beasts, such as sea scorpion and viper and similar, then the corrosion is at the head of the finger, so cut, and do not give it space to reach up to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it reaches the hand, cut at the joint, so that the corrosion does not reach the arm; and if it reaches the arm, cut at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, it is death, and there is no other remedy than to amputate according to its virtue; and thus you do when the corrosion comes or goes: if it comes in the first joint, cut after the other joint; and if it comes in the foot, cut all the foot; and if it rises in the leg, cut at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy than to leave the patient to die; and the manner of amputating or sawing off the member is that you bind above and below, and stretch one minister down below, and another minister up above, and you dissect the flesh between the two ligatures in a spatula-like shape, so that the bone is exposed; then cut or saw, and place a dressing on each part, so that the saw does not touch the healthy tissue, and comes to the patient with another lesion and abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier. de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess on the finger
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe. la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain that comes from the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The two joints that are born in the hands of some men by chance are all flesh, and by chance they have a part where they have bones, and sometimes they have an angle, and none of them are born at the root of the joint, or the birth is not in any of us from the two.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile. Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The sudden pains that come together arise from birth, or from sudden wound, or from burn by fire, or from similar things.

des vils	the bad ones
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	They are gross, swollen veins full of melancholic superfluities that come into many members of the body; and they have more in the legs of those who go on foot and work and carry, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is necessary then that you administer sometimes purging of the intestine, and then the blood of the basilica vein.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The treatment with iron is in two manners: one is that they cut, and draw out the black blood; and the other manner is that you lift the vein, and draw out entirely.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The cutting is according to this manner: first raise the leg with a hot ague very strongly, so that the gross blood becomes subtle, then stretch the leg of the patient from above the thigh just to the part below the knee; then cut the vein in one, two, or three places, with a large cut, then lift and draw out the black blood with your hand, from one end to the other, as much as the virtue of the patient can suffer; and then he lies down, and instructs him to hold fast with black bitter food; and recommence the evacuation and the healing when the veins are full, and annoy the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Here is the translation:
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the vision is contracted and twisted and entwined together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must bend it straight, but do not couple it; and pull it as we have previously said.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The shape of the iron that one uses to couple the vision is curved, and does not cut, so it doesn't couple the vein; and it is a large curve, because if it were subtle, it would couple the vein, but being large as we have said, and this is the shape.
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is engendered in legs, in hot parts where neither herbs nor trees grow, and in earth where there is no moisture; and by chance it grows elsewhere than in legs, and this arises from the putrefaction that comes beneath the skin, as it comes from the serpent-like and worm-like courses within the flesh, engendering between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that a great inflammation comes into the leg, then it changes the joints, and the vein begins to issue forth, just like a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the wound opens, it is necessary that you wrap around a piece of cloth one and a half inches wide up to two inches, and the knot, and leave the cloth on the leg, and every time it does not fall below, if you wrap around the cloth, and the knot; and if it is too long, cut off part of it, and wrap the remainder, and do not cut it at its root, until it is entirely issued; for if you cut it, it returns into the flesh, and brings about abscesses and putrefaction in the limb, and evil disease; because it is necessary that it be treated little by little up to the head, and nothing remains or decays; and there are often times when this vein is treated with five or ten inches long, and a man comes to me who has an issue from ten inches long, and when you cut it, it bursts into the region, and pierces deeply, so that everything issues forth; and let the matter be evacuated which is inside, and apply medicines that prevent putrefaction any day, then cure as for abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And many times at this vein there are many ravings, and similarly when it opens in the joint of the foot, or where the foot is, and a lot of pus comes out, and that's why it often happens; treat the wound thus as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	of wounds that grow between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land "cow's disease", because it often takes hold of the oxen, and is a small wound that grows between skin and flesh, and spreads throughout the body, ascending and descending, and one feels it well from member to member, until it destroys the skin or it becomes a boil; and it is caused by putridity of certain humors, such as worms and serpents and lice and ascariases in the belly; and one doubts its malice, for when it spreads through the body, and it rises to the head, and it reaches the eye, perhaps returns, and destroys the eye; and this often happens.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you want to cure and treat, if one cannot do better than when it was: then it is necessary that you place the limb above and below with a strong, tightly-bound lien, then cut above and treat firmly, and if the vein is deeply embedded in the flesh, and you do not find it, if you cauterize with fire until it dies; and the greatest harm it does, is that it corrupts the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming or approaching near the eye, hold it firmly below with a strong twisted thread, then cut above, and treat firmly; and it is necessary to use the patient's mundification of corporal medicines, solutives for evil humors, and beware of eating bad, rotten food.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and it is a pain that comes into some members, and then moves from member to member; and I saw what I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and I examined her arm, and saw a small inflammation in the vein of the arm; and soon after, I saw it swell up like a vein at the shoulder, more suddenly than anything, like living silver when it runs from one place to another; the pain departed from that place, and fixed itself in the shoulder, and then soon after spread throughout the entire body, until it reached the other arm; then she told me that it returned again throughout her body, as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was very amazed at how it moved in this way from member to member, for I had never seen this illness behave in this manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Everywhere, I had wanted to move the pain from one place to another, but I did not want it, as I saw it in the woman; and I thought that it was because the woman had a dry body, and uncovered veins, and because of this apparent constrained ventilation; and I did not appear according to this reason to those who are delicate, and who have moist bodies and restored veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you want to cure this illness, and the patient feels that pain, it appears as we have said, if the abscess is above and below hastening, and then cope with it until that constriction at the affected area subsides; and cauterize the affected area; and if you do not see it in your eyes, if you cure what drives out the constrictions, such as foul-smelling pills, and pills of serapin, and similar others.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places of the body where they strike.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of them is that there are those with large points, and small ones, and hairy ones, and swollen ones; and those with two angles, and those with tongues, and those where there are pieces; and one which falls in no principal member falls according to several manners: either in a principal member it becomes hairless, such as brain, heart, liver, lungs, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it falls into no place of these limbs, and the sign of death, which I will tell you about afterwards, appears: if it is necessary that you extract this arrow, because death comes afterwards in many dispositions; and when this bad sign does not appear, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then pull it out, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when the arrowhead is in it and pierces the bone, and suddenly the eyes become swollen which are above the brain, is when there is numbness and heaviness and reversal of the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and perturbation of understanding, and vomiting of bile; and perhaps without force from the nostrils, or ears; and perhaps it loses speech and voice; and suddenly the wound becomes a white moist boil resembling a pustule, and suddenly it also breaks out as a bruise of flesh; and if this sign appears, then hold back from treatment, and pull out the arrowhead if it is not inside.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The signs of the swoon when it falls on the heart are that it is near the left nipple, and feels as if it were stuck in a hard thing, not void; and by chance the swoon moves like the pulse, and brings dark black blood, and comes with cold sweat and fainting: thus it is without doubt that death descends.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the signs of the arrow that never leaves the forearm are that without flatulence of scum bursts from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and breathes deeply and seeks the cold region.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrowhead remains in the covering of the thigh, it is beneath the small ribs; and it throws great anguish and great pain and breathes; and moves all the members of the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrowhead remains in the stomach, perhaps it bursts from the wound some undigested food matter.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrowhead is in the chest or belly, and there is no escape from the intestine's route, then there is no hope for a cure, nor in the extraction of the arrowhead.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrowhead is in the bladder, and the urine flows out and comes forth, and the patient feels severe pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limb, as with the face and the neck and the throat and the shoulder and the joint and the spine of the back and the forearm and the elbow and the legs, and the similar limbs, are safe according to several dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrowhead is in a nerve or an artery, and it is not venomous, thus I will tell you what happened to me, because that's how you should do otherwise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to a man that a swoon fell on his arm in the root of the nail: I held it, and drew it from another part beneath the fat of the ear, and was without numbness.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And I drew out a swoon that fell in the fat of the eye beneath the papyrus beneath, and the swoon was restored, and could not reach more than the tip towards the hollow of the fist, and it was a large swoon of a Turkish bow, with all the iron lighter without ears; the game was healthy, and no bad accidents happened to me.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And I pulled out an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and it was an Arabic arrow to the ears: I sewed up the wounds, and subtly touched until I pulled it out, and the Christian was healthy.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And I pulled out an arrow from a man, which had struck him in the belly, and I thought he would die; and then after thirty days had passed, his condition did not change; I cut around the arrow, and extracted it, and pulled it out strongly, and there was no bad accident.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you see a man whose arrow fell near his back, and the wound was swollen above; and the arrow remained inside him, and did not change its natural disposition, nor did he find harm in any of his natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And I saw another man, who was hit by an arrow in his face, and the wound was swollen; and he remained thus without suffering great pain; and many other similar things.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And I treated a wound on the hand of the prince's king, which was swollen in the nail, and it was slightly leaning to the right side; and the wound was completely reposed. I was called for the treatment after it had been swollen for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very constricted.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I sought it with a subtle touch, and did not feel anything; and it felt numbness and pain beneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was from the point of the wound. I put on the location a plaster attractant and digestive, because the wounds did not inflame; and it appeared to me as the wounds of the wound.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I put the plaster on for many days, and the wound reopened, and the patient remained thus for a long time, until he felt the wound one day in his nose; and he told me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I put the medicine corrosive ointment on the wound with my own hands for a long time until it was completely covered, and I felt it, and sensed the head of the arrow which had stuck in the flesh; then I adjusted the opening of the wound with that medicine ointment, so that the head of the arrow appeared visible; and it progressed well within three months, and then I released if the wound that I had touched the tendons, and one part and another, and could not issue; therefore I did not cease from subtly manipulating and ingenious contraptions until I took it out on a good day with well-made tongs, according to what its form would come in the end of this chapter, so that I might pull it out and restore the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the mirror showed that the cartilage of the nose could not be restored: I therefore restored it, and the wound was sewn up, and the entire patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Now you have told about the quality of extracting some arrows, if you put your cure on those that I do not say, for the books cannot take everything; but wise masters compare well a little great thing, and on what is present and failing, they find new work, and new instrument, in the descent of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that the arrows do not issue from the limbs where they are fixed unless according to two manners: either by the place where they enter, or by another part; and the one that jumps forth where it enters is an arrow entering into the flesh, and it does not come out at all now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not come out now, let it be until the flesh is completely porous around, and its exit is eased; and also if it is fixed in the bone, and it cannot come out, let it be thus for some days, and soften it every day; and then it will come out, and if it does not come out, pierce around with a subtle instrument, as much as the flesh around is enlarged, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head, and goes just to one of the ventricles of the brain, and some of the accidents that I have mentioned above to the patient: do not remove it, but let it be until it is even after some days, for if the arrow comes up to there, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is not stuck deeply in the bone, and does not come up to there, and the patient remains for some days without bad accident, then prepare to remove it.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is very stuck in and cannot issue forth, if you administer tar waters within, as I told you; then heal the limb until it is healthy.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is embedded in the body so that it cannot be seen, then search for it everywhere; and if you feel it, remove it with a suitable instrument; and if you cannot do so due to the narrowness of the wound, and the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone or nerve, then make the wound as large as possible; and remove the arrow if you can, and if it has ears that hold it, then cut away the flesh that is attached in two places, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow, so that you can remove it; and be careful not to break the arrow, so that you can remove it more easily.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot at one time, let it remain until the surrounding flesh is purified, then extract it, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the blood flows back, make it contrary, so amend what we have said about the treatment in its chapter; and beware of the incision on the nerve and the vein, and set up a device so you can draw out the arrow without danger, whether fast or slow, or firmly or gently; and place the patient according to the form they were when the arrow fell, for it is the greatest aid that it be, and if you cannot, so arrange it according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another part, where it appears as nothing of it, or the skin is swollen in the area if one sees or feels a sign: cut then above, so much that the tongs can grasp, and then extract: if it does not come out now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is retained in the bone, turn your hand roundly so that it enters into the bone, and enlarges the bone, then pull it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, leave it still, and then recommence the extraction until it comes out; and if the remainder of the arrow is there, push it all the way in; and if the remainder breaks, and you see to administer a push, if you push the instrument gently, so that the point of the arrow enters the hair of the instrument; and then push out, and if the arrow is broken, push the instrument to the point entering inside, to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is touched, it is necessary that you cut around the whole flesh where the veins are, so you can, then heal the wound as it fits.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow falls in the foot or belly or bladder or ribcage, and it is close by, and you can cut above, so you cut; and beware of cutting into a vein and nerve, and then extract, and then sew up the wound, as the craft demands; and heal until it be sound.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tongs with which one extracts arrows is similar to a bird's beak, and you see its shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways: large, moderate, and small, according to the quantity of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the instrument for extracting is like the claw of an eagle's foot, to grasp at the point of the arrow, as it is the shape.
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of the tongs for pushing and for extracting, that's how it is:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the veins of the common body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are 31 veins from which one bleeds, of which the head has 16, namely: two that are behind the ears, called "herbech"; and the two arteries that appear in the temples; and two veins that are in the eyebrows, called "aspires"; and the vein that is on the forehead; and the vein that is at the head of the nose; and the two gullet veins that are in the neck; and the two veins that are above the mouth, and these are the veins called "augeherich"; and two veins that are beneath the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	Here is the translation:
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the vein called "salvatelle" is the one between the auricular and anular, and there are two veins; and in the leg and foot there are three veins: one is below the bend of the left shin, and the second vein which is at the ankle of the right shin; and the vein called "nesse", which is at the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg there are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The vein behind the ears helps with ancient catharrhes and migraines; and the quality of the vein, as I tell you, is that you raise the head of the patient, and rub the place where the veins are like a rough cloth; then hold the patient's neck at an angle, so that the two veins appear behind the ears in their dependent state from the head: take care to do it correctly, and where you feel the pulse beneath your finger, it is a sign of an illness; then take the lancet, and pass it underneath the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand above the whole vein, and cut and peel away the skin and vein, making two holes to traverse, and make the blood flow until you see it; then hold and bind, until it is healthy; and I have already said about incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	Here is the translation:
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The wisdom of the vein at the forehead is worth as much as the wisdom of the cephalic as ancient diseases of the face, and migraine, and redness; and the quality is that the patient strains their neck by twisting, so much that the vein appears; then take the instrument called "fosseur", which has this form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And put the point on the vein, and press with your hand, or something else, and let the blood flow out according to the quantity that you see; then release the patient's neck, and hold the vein until it is healthy and no longer swollen from a large flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not necessary that the flames be too sharp; and the vein of the crossing, because the bone is near, and by chance breaks the flames when they are subtle.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The wisdom of the two veins that are in the two temples helps with eyes, and the brow, and redness, and the pupil in the eye, and diseases of the face; and the quality of their wisdom is that the patient strains their neck by twisting without any thread, as before; then it heals, and let the wisdom of the crossing be a little from the long flame, a little large, for there is no point of burning.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the veins are subtle, perhaps they will break; then make a correction of the blood, as much as you have mastery, and then place it on the cushion, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The vein's health is not so valuable if it is affected by a bitter humor, and if it is over-extracted, and if it has facial diseases, such as emigraine and roujor that comes into the face, and especially when it is old; and the quality of the vein's health is that the patient strains his neck, then strains his nostrils with his left hand, and takes a subtle flame long enough, and inserts it in the space between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well, and the blood will now start to flow; and do not pass too much in front, and make it flow according to your need, then leave it for one night, for it is very quickly restored; and that is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The health of the two gullet veins helps with the constriction of the wing-shaped [part], and at the beginning of messelerie, and many diseases, and empetygin, and corroding, and herpes, and similar things; and the quality of the vein's health is that the patient strains his neck beneath one and the other, as we have said; and so the master stands on the head of the patient, and the patient sits on a seat, then clears the vein of the long tube somewhat widely, then draws blood at the right time, or as much as needed; then repeats another treatment on the other vein, then releases the ligature, and holds both veins moderately, so the patient does not strangle; and leaves it until morning, that the wound may be healthy.
de la sainie des leivres	of the health of the liver
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The health of the veins above the liver helps in the collection at the mouth, and corruption of gums, and cracks of the lips, and painful nose and interior.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the quality of the health is to make the patient sit in front of you, and hold his neck as I have said; then turn the liver, and look at the two veins, one on the right lobe and the other on the left, and recognize them by their blackness, and by the fact that around them there are small black veins: so touch one and the other, and if you do not recognize them, and you are in doubt, then touch the larger part of each, and do the same with the two veins that are above and below, for it is a similar manner.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the health beneath the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The health of the veins that are beneath the tongue helps after the health of the head, and it is at the narrowness of the throat, and for diseases of the eye, and for diseases of the mouth; and the quality of the healer is that the patient sits between your hands before the sun, and lifts the tongue, and looks beneath on each side a black vein: so touch one and the other, and do not go too deep in front, for beneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins that are cut, which are commonly touched, are sensed in two ways: either by pricking the whole flame deeply, or by subtly probing like a cutting trench, and is called "anesil"; and they are large and subtle according to the largeness and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the flame burning so is very renowned, and it is large as if you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is a task to open the veins full of large, apparent blood, and that contain large blood and turmoil; and this is the form of the subtly probing flame.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it's more subtly pointed, and is for clearing the subtle veins, where there is subtle citrus blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The vein of the basilica, which is one of these veins, aids in illnesses that are beneath the throat, and at the neck, and at the chest, and at the belly; and it behooves the healer to bleed severely, and to beware of the artery that is beneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he cuts the artery, and a flow of blood comes, it is necessary to staunch it, as I have said; and one should not prick the flame, but rather cut in a subtle way like "anesil".
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilic vein does not open clearly, it is necessary that you extract it, and change to another; or you want some ease from it, or you heal in its place the opened vein in the arm: it opens clearly; and the treatment with a gentle flame, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you want to recognize the place of the wound, it is necessary also that you extract the arm, so that you touch the place as much as you recognize the pulse; then mark the place of the incision, and then the arm, and treat with a gentle flame; and beware that you do not strike into the artery when you see the place inflamed, for it is an artery: avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it rising high like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and subtle, know that it is from an artery: hurry then, and place your finger there for a long time, then remove your finger if the blood stops; treat the arm thus, and let it be, and do not move the patient; and be on guard, and do not move until they are healthy.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the blood is not stagnant, and it flows, and the medicine is not present, then cut into the artery so that it opens, for the head of the vein returns; and stagnates the blood.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a fist-sized bandage, and wrap it around, and take one of the medications and place it just next to the other wound; if the bleeding stops, that's good; if not, then treat with powders that stop blood, as we have said; and the stopping of bleeding is not troublesome in many dispositions for the small wound of the arm, and the possibility of a strong bond from the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The vein on the wrist is so helpful if it draws blood from the head above, and from the body below, because it is composed of basilic and cephalic, as we have said; and it behooves the healer to be careful about the nerve that lies beneath, and not to cut too deep, lest he injure the nerve, and cause swelling and pain, and perhaps cannot heal; and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in any homes due to its subtlety, then it behooves you to sound the vein with your instrument carefully; and avoid the nerve at all cost.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if he has a vein between the two fingers, then make it bleed far away.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The sanity of the head helps, which attracts blood from the chief, and helps the eyes; and it is necessary to anoint the olive oil flame or the myrtle flame, because it is the safest of all the veins, since it has no nerve nor artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	Always, it is necessary to choose the lightest vein, and not to harm anything if one fails the first time, and one starts again; and sometimes it inflames the veins of some men, as if one failed the first time, but it does not harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the health is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about anointing is that anointing is not administered for the sake of keeping health, but to prevent future diseases; and it should be done in one of the three veins that are on the arm: namely, cephalic, basic, and basilic; and one should anoint at the beginning of spring, autumn, and winter after eating, when signs of fullness appear; and one should anoint on the first day or third day, after two hours or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The healthy person who is administering to the sick has no fixed hour determined, but only when need is from day or night, in all hours and in every tense; and it is not suitable for a healthier person to cure children up to 13 years old, nor a woman carrying fruit beyond four months until seven.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor should they be cauterized, the old who have passed 60 years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when someone wants to heal, in whatever manner it may be, it is suitable for them to purge the intestines with a lighter clyster, if they have retained many bad humors, so that the veins do not attract the superfluous and harmful humors from the principal members; nor does one heal who is too full of food, or drunk, as long as they are furious, nor dropsical; and beware of healing after colic passion, and vomiting, and stomach discomfort, and multiple births in a woman, and labor, and watching, and juning, and all virtues, either by the arm or the body; then subtle humors, if the blood is thick, through food and drinks and medicines, so you have little power; then enter into a bath, since nothing can deflect it, to subtly purge the blood, and heal from the vein of the thigh up to the third, as we have said; and guard against that day of labor, and point, and luxury, and similar things; and be cheerful and joyful, and let the healer be higher than the one being healed, and rub the arm II or III times, then gently stretch the limb upwards, for when it is too stretched or bent, it cannot correct the blood; and then rub the hand many times until the veins swell, and feel them; then anoint the healer with a little oil of a small vial, then put their left hand under that vein up to the elbow where they want to heal, so that the vein does not flee and fail at the touch.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	Because there are veins that flee like cords to the sane, and if there are those that are full of windiness, so when one puts on the flame, it draws back from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus is one of these; and if it opens the vein, so is the wound too narrow, because it is necessary that the sane people be warned about these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens for the first time, it is good; if not, then recommence a little below that place or at the joint, so the veins are not inflamed.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the veins are inflamed, and the patient is frightened, leave it a day or two, and do not bind the arm: perhaps abscesses will form; do not enter or bathe, then resume the treatment as it pleases; and if the perforation is small, or the blood flows subtly and you doubt that there is not so much blood as you see, pierce into that same perforation all the way straight; and open a little hastily, thus the veins are inflamed; for this happens often, when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the limb swollen, do not restart the health, and put a little oil of oleum on it, for it alleviates the body's pain of blood, and is mended in this limb with the oil; and thus administer the oil of oleum in each health that you heal the veins, to staunch the flow of blood; and this same thing makes threefold and bulging eyes, when one puts it on the limb; if one subtly feels the vein and separates when it is too large.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if a large abscess comes, which often happens, especially when it is not healthy unless at that time when the opening of the vein is small, hurry, and put on the limb a moist sponge in water and a little hot, and hold for an hour; and it is necessary to do this after the blood issue from the vein, and if it remains on the limb after some days without any blackness or greenness, do not touch it; and if you see, put on some thing of aloe or myrrh remedy in juice of camomile, monstastre, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times there is an abscess and appearance at the wound of the basilica: put your hand on it, and if you find the soft spot at the pressure of the hand, then it is that bad appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid then that you do not put on anything of what we have said, for by chance it will cut short without deartering; but make the wound a little deeper to harden the spot, then apply another treatment, until it is healthy.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And bleed each one of blood according to the quantity of its virtue, and of the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it issue forth until it becomes red; and if you see it thick, let it flow until it becomes subtle; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is necessary for the one who is full and strong to have a blood extraction done with a larger wound, and let the flames be large; and for the one who is weak, do the opposite, and make the wound smaller and more frequent, and you must heal in a diagonal direction, not by pricking; and this method of healing is free from decay of blood and copiousness of nerve, and is worth more than the healing done at length or width.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for the one whose body needs healing, it is necessary to give a warm poultice made from juice of green apples; if they are overheated, then draw out three or four times the amount of blood; and if they have a cold complexion, then apply before the healing a warm poultice made with muscadine syrup, or aromatic honey syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.
